O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You dear children, I have completed this book which is the culmination of medical knowledge collection and compilation, finishing it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And in my vision, I thought of completing it with this manual tool, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is highly practiced in our region and spread everywhere, if the science has been lost or abandoned, there are no longer any remnants from it other than small descriptions found in books written by the ancients that were used with the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, errors and vanity have arisen, and closed minds occur, causing the loss of knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I can revive this treatise together with its arrangement, according to the path of exposition and declaration, and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will bring together the forms of the metal cauteries and other tools of surgery, along with their appropriate arrangement and preparation for use, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled physicians can be found in our times, the art of medicine has been lost.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	It is necessary that one who interferes in this matter become proficient in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as they understand the position of the limbs, their shapes and connections and separations, have knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles, know the number of bones, the movement and location of mobile and stationary veins, and the origin of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And this is what Hippocrates said: we lack nothing with knowledge, and yet we are poor with work;
et meismement en l’art de main.	In the art of manual skills as well.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone is unaware of what has been said before, they may fall into error and misuse others;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Just as I have seen many who interfere with this science and abandon their studies without experimenting;
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish doctor who treated a lymph node or sore throat on a woman's neck, and also cut her arteries from the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood flowed out that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And saw another doctor treating a stone in an old man's kidney, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he took out with it a piece of the bladder, and he died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to draw blood, and saw the arrangement of the body part and the size of the stone, and if he had let me cut him it would have led to his death.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And saw another doctor who treated our local duke whose leg was broken, and with the breaking there was an injury;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the doctors, full of ignorance, allowed the breaking to occur on the wound like it was done by strong joy, and did not allow any healing for the injury, and let this end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commands not to dislocate it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And wait like the leg was fully grown and the feet, leading to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I hurry to come to him, and quickly rush to dislocate the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And when I hear it dislocated so smoothly without any pain being felt.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the corruption was already confirmed or member, and could not be cured;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And the corruption continued to spread through the member until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another mark that collapses an abscess, then inflames it due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a gangrene, when it is full of melancholic humours, it should not be touched with iron if it has not been cut in such a way that all that is corrupted can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, dear children, you need to know that the art of surgery is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that means, surgery where there is danger in multiple positions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And I will show you in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary that you keep them, so that the foolish might not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your weapons in caution, and treat your ailments lightly yet firmly, and employ the best means so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and remain healthy;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the terrifying diseases without relief for health;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien declares in none of these admonishments:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Never take a remedy for an illness when you're not called crazy by your fellow villagers.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters deal with fire cautery and medicinal cautery, and are arranged from the head down to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the shapes of the instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything else that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and these chapters are arranged with the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it is organized according to the location of the head up to the elbow, and regarding the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remind ourselves of the work, it is fitting that I describe the quality of each remedy and its harm for each constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, is the longest speech and subtlest science and the hidden answers;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And many wise ones spoke about this, agreeing with it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And they find my words insufficient, for I fear the length of it.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the cautery helps universally in all constitutions where there is matter, for there are two types of constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This means knowing that the hot constitution has matter and the dry constitution also has matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In the combination of hot and dry constitutions with matter, they devised something and said that the cautery is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And the other said otherwise:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that the cautery is only good for illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be treated with hot illnesses by heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And this person who said the opposite states that the cautery provides great help to hot and dry illnesses that come from within the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the condition of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true every time by experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And through any means, do not interfere except for the one who has experienced it, and who knows from long use of the chapter on cauteries, and the variety of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and duration;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	For other complexions we have nothing more to say, especially in matters of cold and wet illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them gathered together with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my children, that the assembly of a fire cautery has secrets in healing, and brings more benefit than a burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it only affects the limb that is being treated, not harming any other limbs if properly done.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines spread from one body part to another upon application, causing diseases if not properly treated;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance they bring the injury to the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and due to the goodness of its substance does not do this thing if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And I have found this through experimentation and the length of my service and study in the art, it was based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this I apologize for the length of my words, because it does not please me to disclose the secret which is revealed by fire and the quality of the work, how it removes diseases from the body, as the philosopher explains in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they agreed on what times the cauterizations should be made, and set fire to them.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that the cautery is suitable in all circumstances, for the nuisances arising are greatly mitigated by the aid of the cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And indeed, if the cautery is for necessary pains beyond and after which cannot wait until a greater mischief befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think it, dear boy, as do those foolish lookers-on;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery does not recur;
et il le dient ensi;	and he says it thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	But it is not as they think, for the cautery is but a medicine that modifies the complexion and dries out the fluids causing pain. It is worth more than medicines due to its speed in enhancing its value and the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And things that can happen is that the disease will come at any time according to the composition of the patient's body and the location of the illness and its nature;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And it happens that excesses accumulate in him through the acquisition of meats and similar things; if this is not treated with a cautery where there's excess moisture or dampness, such as hot cauterizations for pain, and similar things, then such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And few understand why cauterizations are called the last of medicine; it's something to be seen.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they don't believe that cauterizations are to be used after medicine; their understanding is false. Cauterizations are the last resort in medicine because when our methods of treatment fail in any illness and do not work, then we administer a cauterization, and it proves effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it's clear that cauterization is part of medicine, not according to the thoughts of ignorant people though.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The old ones said that cauteries of gold instruments are more effective than those made of iron, and they stated this because of the quality of gold and due to its high quality substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the metal of the cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not visible; it's just a statement because I have experimented with it and found out that indeed it becomes visible in some individuals.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Gold cauteries are better than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet, when you heat an iron instrument, you may not notice it being heated by the color of the gold, and then suddenly it cools down.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is overheated;
si font au feu;	if they use the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus I have enough obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And that is why we use iron cauterization tools that we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	And you have ordered this chapter on the animal's head up to the nose, because its visibility is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	For the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive cautery is effective against moisture and cold in the brain, and there are two ways to do it due to an illness called 'soda', and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothaches, throat pain, and especially all diseases caused by cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be cleansed with a solvent medicine, altering the body's three humors or four, depending on how well the properties and heat and habit of the patient can endure it;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then restore the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make them sit cross-legged between your hands, and place their feet on a hard surface;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his second fingers;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and when your thumbs reach there, if blood flows from the nose then warm the cautery called "olive" which has this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it at its proper position with ink as a mark, and make your way down and hold your hand gently and gradually while adjusting.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then ease your hand slightly, and check if you can see the bone when it moves a little;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see it, start the cautery again until you see the bone as I have instructed;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking some wool, prepare and make it soft inside, then place it at its proper position, and let it be for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After put butter on moist cotton;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	And leave it until the scab is completely dried off;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treat the wound with ointment known as 'tetrafarmac', until it heals properly.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And those who were of old would say, that when a wound is left open longer, more purges out;
et por ce si aide mues.	and because of this, the help moves.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that we must let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burned, and then reset the one that has been burnt by the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And those who say otherwise state that the cautery should be applied and pressed as long as necessary, and push so hard on it until you can displace bone like a finger that women use when they are pregnant; because fluids should flow out from this.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	And must the wound be left open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After that, one should clean and dry it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to be good for all purposes, except in certain cases where there is a risk of infection;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	And it seems to me that I should let it alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the head of the shoulder is weakened by continuous exposure to nature's substances, as we testify regarding other members.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And indeed when the shoulder head is weak due to nature, and the first sign of a cautery is more healing for me, and from this I work thus assembling together a cure.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From old age pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain in the head occurs and lasts for a long time, one should use the patient's ears and pills which are called "couchie," and also perform cleansing of the head and ears and apply bandages;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And if one performs the cautery as we have previously mentioned, it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the shoulder of the sick person is of strong constitution, and do not let it be too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Therefore, treat with a small fire cautery as we have described above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After you perform the cautery on each hoof up to the bone, as we said before, and do the cautery where the bone is called 'vessel';
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and place there what one uses for suction cups;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	Move your hand so that you do not see until the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels too much greater pain in this cautery compared to others, and I will speak about it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	It is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than that of the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	The fire cautery commands the patient to let his hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When pain suddenly comes in part of the head, and extends to the eye, and the shoulder is cleared by purifying medicines, and other treatments have been done as I said in the section on diseases, and nothing benefits:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Therefore apply cautery according to two methods, namely using medicinal heat and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauteries using medicinal heat involve taking a dose of oil, and removing the bark and coating it over the two heads, then apply it around where the pain is located in such a way that you can place the oil right under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it has been placed, if it adheres well and you keep it in place for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	Then remove the oil bandage and remove the garlic oil, and leave the wound for two days or three;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then place a butter poultice on it until heat comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the ointment treatment as long as it is effective;

Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head takes on the shape of an oxen horn where there is a slight curvature at the beginning and a small appearance in the middle;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it in the painful area, hold your hand and gently twist the iron, until half of the tip of the key is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and let your hand rest so that no artery burns and it opens, allowing an abundance of blood to flow.

puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put moistened cotton in butter, and then apply ointment to the wound until it is clean;

de emigraine	Of the headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously discussed in the divisions of diseases, and if it doesn't improve, and you observe that the cauterizations mentioned earlier from medical knowledge do not affect this migraine, then you should heat up the cautery called 'cultellare' until it becomes white.

et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And be wary of the jaw that clamps shut when chewing, and ensure there is only silence in the mouth, with no spasms affecting the patient. mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it happens in this book.

de la torture de la bouche	of the torment/pain in the mouth

de litargie	of liturgy

de la froidor dou chief	from cold of the head

de l’epilempsie	From the cautery

dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that touches the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	No time has it happened that the hair of the oils turns into fat and grabs the oil, and then one performs cauteries according to two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	This means knowing either fire or burning medicine.

aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After scraping until it is clean.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle:

de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary for you to apply cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place their head in your good health;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and guide the surgeons' heads between your hands in such a manner that they do not move and do not lose their heads;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after this, put in an egg or myrrh juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heat up the cautery which is made of metal:

mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but still, this is what should be done for your work.

Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then apply the fire cautery again once or if needed, and leave it for three days.

de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess on the throat

dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth

de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from coldness, or there is coldness or fever, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it requires cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	The fire cautery made from butter is such that you take cow's butter, and at the tip use a spoon made of iron or anointing stick;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, soak in butter until it's saturated, then place it over the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools down.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And do this often until the butter's properties reach the root of the tooth. If you see wet wool and cotton saturated in cold butter, place them over the aching tooth, and hold it on hot iron until the heat reaches the gum around the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery made from iron or anointing stick is such that you take it, and make it large enough so the heat does not reach the skin of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, from which its form will come afterwards, place it on the teeth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be alleviated either that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patients fill their mouths with good butter in anticipation of the heat of the cautery, and then quickly remove it.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:

de la toust	Of cautery by fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

de ydropisie	Regarding dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery does not work in dry conditions, except for the method that is called "asclytes".

et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would hasten, and both intentions together with God's help.

de l’enfleure des piez	regarding the swelling of bones

de la cure des emorroydes	Of treatments for hemorrhoids

de la dolor de la hainche	From thigh pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes in the thigh region, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient's condition has been treated as we have described in the division of diseases and treatment does not work, and the illness is old:

c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Here is what you need to know, it consists of hot remedies and fire cautery.

que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	You should apply the cautery on the hip's bony prominence with three triangular cauterizations following this shape. mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But do it in this manner so that the circles contain all the hip, and all the nerves leading to the heart be cut.

et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is around the knee towards the thigh, then you do the cautery with a cutaneous or circular fire iron and make sure to take great care in all your cauteries that you do not allow the heat for too long, burning nerves and major arteries, and that you cause no more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the surgeon said about the cautery of the hip, as follows: make it such a device and have its head as thick as a finger joint, or slightly less, and let there be crosspieces and place them from one crosspiece to the other distance equivalent to the size of a small handful.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	And let the crosspieces be made in two parts and also be like knots, and it should have a well-made iron handle;
et c’est li forme:	And this is its form:

Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The medical hot irons are such that you make an instrument of interweavings in which descends the edge of the door, and may be of iron or steel with one long surface, and at its height have two holes, and between each have the size increase of a finger;

et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	This is the way of hot application, and I have written it down as an appendix to this medical treatise.

Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then there will be plenty of water and administered in motion of medical operations and in cauterizations of other limbs.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And it performs equal work as fire, and for other medicines which are used in cauterizations of the hip like mustard oil and resin with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment in which an honored person was treated for the pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and with great relief. He says that no other treatment was done, and that it cured him completely in one fell swoop when this treatment was performed, and he bathed himself as he instructs hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And instruct them in this manner that you take green, fresh and dry lead tar, grind it very finely with a little fat, and spread it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is located, and bind it;
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and leave it for three hours, and by the quantity that the disease no longer feels the burn.

And then make them enter into a bath as long as their body becomes somewhat refreshed, and make them enter onto bed, and the pain will disappear completely and they shall be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	Know that no one should use such medicines as a cautery, if it isn't after the removal of flesh.
