et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And pull nothing from the threads with it, then place the cap on the instrument, as described here which seems like force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And always the head is bent, and one place to another, and it's very sharp, made of iron or finely crafted metal:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument at hand, then shape it with pliers, which should resemble the form described above:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And being cut from one side, and from the other side name;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner, and after cutting gargle the raw wounds with hot water, or hot and mild water. If there is bleeding during this process, continue to gargle with cold water, or slices of cooked pomegranates peels, or mint leaves, and similar things until the wound has healed.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then continue the treatment as long as it is effective;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And no new abscesses form in the throat other than the two almonds, so cut them similarly as the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely the small one;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And indeed I had almost completely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage and could neither eat nor drink, and she died if she remained like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had required two drains each, at both nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I acted quickly then, and struck one of them with an axe, and after that, the other ran out, and I cut out a large portion of the belly;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I cut into that one from its other nostril, and I looked inside, seeing the tongue and pressing it.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After I struck them in those abscesses and scraped out some parts, only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus the woman's throat passage was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, not stopping her until I continued to cut into that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscess would reappear immediately, filling up again the space I had emptied, until it reached a size that was not very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Therefore, I gaged and cauterized inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Then it would not re-grow;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I left those parts alone, may only God have made them after me.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the rumen descends to the ovum, and it is elongated and long, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is outside large and round, it is called "ovum".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the ointment for the abscess has calmed down, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to take her.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	And the one that is round assembled and isn't far;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And if it's reddish or has a coppery hue or is black, you should consider making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, of its blemish and length, you should make the patient stand in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we described earlier;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then insert the onion in the belly, and guide it along, and prepare at the location of the two instruments I said about in the incision of the two almond-shaped glands.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not remove more flesh than the excess beyond the natural boundary;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	For if you do more, you harm with your voice, and by your words;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, apply what we have advised about incisions on the two cheeks, and treat until it has healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if they are in danger from excess, you should apply the instrument of cautery to remove them.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery is done with an incision tool.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And when the patient's head has reached your health, then press their tongue with the instrument we have discussed in the section on fire cautery, and use it with sharp steel blades, so that they are neither too thick nor too thin;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using the power of this tool, as it is described here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let your head receive a hair or where you place the medicine, just like the movements of a spoon, and put the tool over all the medicine on the wound;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And the patient's sides are so sore that he can barely breathe and move his muscles from within his mouth to the medicine, so it doesn't descend into his throat, and he sweats.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the wound, the amount equivalent to half an hour's dosage, until you see the medicine bubbling and the agitation of the medicine subsides.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And when you see this, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, soak the cotton in the medicine, and place the tool with all the cotton on the wick above, until the cotton burns out over the wound.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often, until the cauterizing agent is perfect, then let it dry, and clean after three or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the fire cautery in medicine, then do so, and after the cautery, press inside the eye with a cotton swab soaked in butter, and clean the area that was treated by the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And you should rinse with cold water, or perform gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, without using the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calamus, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile and parsley, and any similar herbs, gather all of them or some of them into a pot, put water in it, and bring it to a boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot place the tool for burning according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And whether made of silver or iron, and whether one of the shoulder blades is placed in the mouth of the patient until the steam rises from the wound through the nose, until the wound has become necrotic;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the process often repeats, until the wound dries, and remember not to do this at the beginning of the abscess's development, for many things happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And don't do this until the abscess is ready to rupture.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cloth and place an eggshell inside the patient's mouth, so that the heat of the wound does not become too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the eggshell does not allow heavy steam to enter the mouth, and this is a good treatment that promotes healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times a foreign object is inserted into the throat bone or spine of fish, or no thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So it follows that you should extract what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what does not allow you to see and is found in the throat, it follows that you should make the patient vomit this way so that the meat becomes cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	By chance if the thing is expelled by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or the object ingested might be an sponge piece, or a belly button piece, or a lettuce root, or a chunk of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	And you attach the thread to the sponge, and then swallow it.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	And when she comes to its place, if it extends, then pull with force;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	And if she does not come by means of what we have said, take the plumb instrument according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And have the instruments bent at its head so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and raise the head high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	And be careful not to touch the epiglottis, that it does not harm him, nor should you push any bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And if the patient pushes the instrument, that's what it means when he moves or if something is slippery;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If it pushes into the mouth, or pulls forcefully with all the instrument equally until it is strong.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the substance of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No treatment is given to those without blood, as I have said in the division, through the cure of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And if this does not benefit, then look into the mouth of the patient towards the sun, and when you press their tongue with the instrument I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vessel, guide it with all your skill, or use delicate forceps that are suitable for this task.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't suffice, take a hairy stick and place it in the throat of the patient, then press where the hair of the stick bends, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you wash the patient with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full cup of cold water, and open the mouth, pour it in gently so they can swallow, and move it often with their hand;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And if soon after the water reaches the blood, it causes them to vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not vomit as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will succeed without fail.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is as follows: you take the pot where there are burning coals and place it under a closely fitted lid in the middle, with the head of the instrument in that space;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then pour in the fumigation, and the patient places the tip of the reed in their mouth, closing it so that no smoke escapes but goes all the way down to the throat;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And now the saliva will flow out, and if it does not, you should repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And let the patient feel thirsty, and have them consume salty things and such, but do not give them water to drink;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And thus, it is necessary for her to depart through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to extract gallbladder bile, if it is seen, resembles curved scissors for moving into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has the appearance of a surgeon's knife, and it has the roughness of a rasp, so whatever she takes, she cannot leave;
et vez ci la forme:	and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	No exact descriptions of pus are given, according to what memory brings up after one and another in this book, they vary in perforation and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and there are two ways to do this, one being in its own appearance and the other due to moisture it holds.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those who have them within their body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the head are different from those on the foundation, and the abscesses on the internal muscle are different from those that come to joints, and each has its judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if dealing with abscesses one must not pierce them until the wound has fully developed according to its natural course;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for such cases it is necessary to pierce when they have grown and do not heal according to their development, like abscesses that lie near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come below joints, if you leave it ripe inside by chance, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes a contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	If the abscess lies near the main limb, and if you delay the puncturing until it is dead, it will harm the main limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	If it lies near the root, if one pierces it or in such a way that it is dead;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is not appropriate to pierce a growing abscess without its natural development being completed, except for the one that lies near the root, which should not rot internally and extend inside, resulting in an internal passage;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And cannot heal properly in a large extent.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary for you to know the time of the abscess perforation which happens with completion, and this is when the pain subsides, and the departure of the fever, and the reduction of the pain and redness, and the beginning movement and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it is necessary for you to position the puncture or more according to the location of the abscess, and wherever it opens moves;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And let the puncture be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on hands or feet, or joints and necks and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases when they bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are within the fatty part of the body, it is better to wait until you have completed digestion before making an incision as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce him before it, so it penetrates his body with the venom from him, and is full of maggots.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance harden the lips and you depress under them.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at no abscesses they puncture across the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you remove small pus pockets, small cuts;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large pus pockets, large cuts, and many wounds according to the size of the pus pocket;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such pus pockets or it is necessary to bleed it, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become as white as a cloth, and is softened, then you must do the same as when dealing with boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such that are split into three corners, and if there are such as are treated like the leaves of myrtle, like boil-like pus pockets;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And if such occur or one makes a round cut, and other cuts and seeming slicing.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those without heads, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them completely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when the abscesses are large, and they have grown significantly in size, if you pierce them, do not drain all the pus at once, but remove a portion of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then numb the abscess up to the other side, then leave nothing untouched thereafter;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this repeatedly from large to small portions until all pus has drained;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Similarly, if the patient has weak immunity, or is pregnant, or young children, or elderly and feeble individuals.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when he tries thrice with the release of the bow, that perhaps kills the patient, and you do not realize this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have identified your abscess, if it has ruptured, observe the wound, and check whether the abscess wound is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it's a flat stitcher, try using linen or vegetable cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it's a large abscess and there are many cavities, it is necessary that you insert a needle in each one so they press against each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have removed a portion of the skin in the abscess and sutured it inward, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen thread ash, and bind it up until the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone, and treat with ointment as long as it remains healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood should start to pour out from your vein, cool it down with cold water and ease it off gradually, and hold the wet cloth there for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if blood loss continues persistently, you must administer control and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned with your hands in this book, and if it's near a vein, or the place where an abscess is, being mostly nervous, then it is necessary for you to put moist tents and cloths soaked in wine and heated oil on them;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it's in the body, and the affected area is fleshly, then it is necessary for you to place moist cloths on them, either in water or oil, or wine and cold oil, up to three days, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove and clean the abscess, following as it should be done, until there is no more pus.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this knowledge should be universally applied in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or you have been told how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and this chapter explains it.
des soros	of the stomach
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	In the head region, small abscesses come about, and their manner is like those on cloths, similarly to a jeweler's work with a catkin, and many have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fat and such where there is moisture as well as pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And for those that are hard and stony to the tailor, and there is no doubt that they have arteries not otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the scalpel is that you must prove it with every instrument which is called 'intermediary', from which the form comes after, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then make the cut above for its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, one scours without leaving anything behind the skin containing that moisture, for it returns immediately once nothing is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it's present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And these run those who remain during the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And repeat the cotton process, just as before, on the second day and the third, until you are sure it does not remain overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply ointment to the wound with what is suitable, until it heals properly.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess remains without pus, shape it according to this form, along its length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and remove your doubts, and burn all around, and apply your entire treatment to the area where it is located;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if it goes against the artery, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly handle the abscess if it is made of stone, and cut and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting on the stone-abscess and the wet one, it is lighter because they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses or heads, and for the pus-filled abscesses that I described or from an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	And I found the abscess just like a soft stone, hard, rough, and white, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if we had missed any, we would have also made the wound just as well like in cutting through a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or going, it was necessary that those coming from the neck and the roots of the ears have their incision open for as long as possible depending on its healing, so that the blood may come out;
et les cure si com il covient.	And treat them according to what is appropriate.
des scrophules	regarding the pock marks
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs in the throat, and close to the glands, and in the necks, and do not come to any other parts or on the body, they are hard, and are entangled with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrophula is properly within its coat, just like the node and the abscess at the neck, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And the appearances of these scrophulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to submit to health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In that situation where you see good condition at the throat, and it appears like the color of flesh, mute from each side and not strangled around the neck or to the artery nor in the duct, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	It is necessary that you treat it from above, and excise each part of it, and have the two lips of the throat at the angle where they meet, if you need to do so, just as we explained in abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Gently and carefully remove it, be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, nor make too much of a mess with blood, let your hands stay in control, do not advance too far, so as not to remove more than what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you have to remove the vein or the artery and it doesn't allow opening, apply vitriol or any powders that coagulate blood to the wound, and restrain the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And let it (the patient) until the abscess is calmed down, and the wound begins to soften, and heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the boy has been healed, then return to your work, until you finish it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then follow the indication of whether there are any small scabs remaining, if you clean and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scab, it doesn't suit to clip that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall away by itself without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then proceed with treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you are dealing with all of the ulceration, it is necessary that you gather together the two lips of the wound, and now suture them, because there should be no excess remaining due to the size of the ulcer.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you understand how to cut into it, drain the pus, and suture it, just as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those excess scabs that remain, pierce them wherever they have opened and let them heal;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And dig as was said before, while depending on it, then he administers remedies with ointment and similar things, so that what is left of the decay can be corrupted.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound has been well cleaned, let the ointment cure the flesh, as long as it is healthy.
de squinance	"De squinance" translates to "on squinting" or "concerning squint". This term could be referring to medical treatments or observations related to eye disorders where one eye may be turned inward (intorsion) or outward (extorsion). The specifics would depend on the broader context of the text that this phrase is found in.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old ones spoke and discussed about the surgery of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	But I never saw anyone do it in our land, and that's how they wrote their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with strabismus, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called "the epiglottis" be avoided;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And do not seek help in this way because all the veins and the heart are near to those with abscesses either inside their mouth or in the throat or under the two kidneys.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is within the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis in order to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to incise the epiglottis, it should be cut through at three or four small cuts in between two circles. By the size of these cuts according to their depth, not within the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And such cuts are compatible for the division of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the blood vessels are long along it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to all the inch, then cut out the lump until it reaches the bone;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And avoid blood vessels, if you see nothing, then cut out the sore, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the rupture of the stream in the bone that leaps out through the limb which has been broken, and due to the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the time has passed in which one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound like a mouth, and sew it all smoothly without touching the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that promote strength until they become clear.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albacus suggests that one should not perform this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged dead, and the deficiency has been made.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore hold the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe normally, and they are breathing through the wound, and thus is protected from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And because they were commanded by the ancients to leave the wound open until the illness's malady passes, and it passed in three days or four. And then they ordered to stitch up the wound and clean it, while it was being cleaned;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took a knife and stabbed it into her throat, and cut some of the channels leading to the heart;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and it was well that she did not have a cut vein or artery but rather the wind flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I rushed, and treated the wound, and cured her until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and only had to rest for the maiden's voice to recover, and she returned after that to her usual state of health;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore, I say that in the surgery for the tailoring of the epiglottis, there should not be hesitation.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These abscesses are called "neck hernia", and they are large abscesses in the color of a chestnut, and are very common among women;
et est selonc II manieres:	And according to two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	naturally, and by chance;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural has no illness.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents occur in two ways, of which one is similar to our fat and the other way is like an abscess that comes from our blood.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it should not open for surgery except in cases that are small, and the proof and search apply to every intervention:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as large as our fat and cannot reach any vein, cut it out, just like we would cut out our fat, and treat it with all its boundaries, if there is any part;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search thoroughly immediately, then treat as appropriate until it is completely healed.
des nous	from nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are available to us, of which I will say all the equivalents;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary for me to explain all the differences that exist between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that disease is characterized by fever and warmth until the ebullitions have passed and putrefaction has been completed;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	So, the fever and heat then subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the healthy body has no heat, fever, or pain, and contains lymph, which is its own sac and follows the color of the flesh, and begins also like a boil, and becomes swollen;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and according to two appearances, or fatty, or moist, and much of the color is as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a new injury, that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called 'intermediary', according to whether their shape appears or after chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of incision into abscesses is that you take or more moist than you find within the abscess, and move your hands little by little, until you know that the instruments have reached the core, then proceed according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the pus, and take care that no spill occurs.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture is clear and of what color it is, cut it as I've said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if no pus comes out after the pus, know that it is fatty, then cut it diagonally, and take hold of it with forceps, and gently scrape each side of it. Keep the cloth where the pus lies to pull out a healthy one with the knot;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot bring it back healthy, so take it piece by piece until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if there is nothing left, the body will return through many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if only a little remains and it doesn't bother you, use some corrosive powders on the wound, keep the wound in place, apply things that calm abscess heat, and treat with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the body is large, so cut both lips of the wound, and treat with those who are in charge of surgical procedures.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the vein is too small or another if you hurry, use the inside of the ashes in powder form, and let it sit for 2 days or 3, until the wound heals, and rest with blood boiling.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to consider what has been delayed by the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of the surgical instruments that are used together, and they are in three ways:
grans et moien et petit;	large ones and medium-sized ones and small ones;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three sizes of them which are called 'albaret', and one that is called 'breb', and they come in three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium-sized, and small ones, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like needles from which one sews veins, and they can be of citrine quill, or iron, or silver, and golden ones are preferred because black wax is more effective for encircling the bends of a fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	And there are three ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Large ones, medium ones, and small ones, according to the amount of width in the cuts.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the thorns are like some resemblance, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Large ones, medium ones, and small ones;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are thorns with two curves in three ways such;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are thorns with three curves, and they are also in three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are thorns with two curves, and single-curved thorns only, and they are in three ways;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	All of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of this one to whom you make your cutting tool, and there are such who do not cut force but from one side, which we burn the skin, because here one does not cut the vein nor the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these introducers have their handles attached with clamps, so that the patient does not lose them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three ways:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	largely, small, and moderate, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and none of them uses force only in the lower part, such as legs and arms, breasts, and joints, and similar body parts;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and there is no other small instrument similar to the surgical blades, resembling stumps of nails, according to this shape, with which one stops bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it should never be placed at the site of a healthy artery or veins, and under no circumstances follow this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At times, the nipples of some men swell when they begin to become corrupted, until they seem like female nipples.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	And remain disfigured and swollen. If one wishes to treat them, they should do so according to this form of this line .b. until .g..
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strip the fat, apply medicine to the wound that promotes healing, then stitch together the two edges of the wound, and continue treatment until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if the nipple leans downwards, and is flattened due to its size, like it happens in women, if they divide it into two parts above, by two similar slits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From which one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then burn the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have instructed about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in treatment, as long as they are healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healthy, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient cannot rest, or due to bleeding, you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive salve;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it as long as it can chew with the mouth and swallowing the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	removal of abscesses from the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Wounds that come from abscesses are manners of hard scrophules where there are nodes, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g:.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, you should fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses resemble scrophules, cut them as we have said in cuts on scrophules, and if the wound is full of pus, apply a cautery as we have said previously.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin above it has been sewn together, there are many times when abscesses occur, and similarly, this happens with the drained vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows it thus when it is due to an artery, then are the abscesses long and filled completely;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	And when you feel it with your fingers, if there's a constriction;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when it's due to the vein, then expect discolored fluids;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it's madness to cope with this abscess, and similarly when it appears on the sides and at the angles and under the collarbone and in many other parts of the body, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid the iron treatment, and that which is at the head also needs to be avoided, and for him who has an inflamed artery, do it above the skin until long;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work on the twelve inches, and beautifully remove the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then take out of the person a needle, and make it pierce until the other side, and bind the artery with a doubled thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in extracting the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then puncture the area between the two ties with an introducer until blood flows from where there was a clot, and release the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the treatment that requires blood flow, as long as the knot is present;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this with ointment attached to it, until it becomes clean;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is as large as the vein, you should mark with your hand what part of the abscess you can reach on the skin. Then take out the needle from the area held in your hand and make it pierce through, using a doubled thread, so that you bring it to the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then remove the abscess, as I told you, or tie one of two parts at each shoulder with a string;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the threads will hold, if I sew another needle to each end of all four threads across the entire abscess at the incision point for the first needle, and secure the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess as much of the excess comes out, then trim away the remaining excess carefully and leave what is tied up;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place on the cloth a moist mixture of wine and oil, then administer treatments and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	The removals of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, when an abscess forms in the artery and vein, abscesses also form on nerves when they are cut, or due to excessive labor, and similar conditions.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens with shoulders and elbows and in all places where joints are present, it's the case for abscesses, and its color seems like flesh color, and is felt in various positions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is constrained to form, the patient feels great pain, and is not satisfied by the fullness of the body, but rather experiences discomfort in the belly;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And moves in all directions, neither forward nor backward, neither up nor down, and the one in joints does not fit to be covered with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	By chance it would undergo contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And that which is in the head or forehead, makes the skin sweat out.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If abscesses are small, then with your forceps, you grasp them at their base;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, then suspend it at the anus, and cut it open, and remove the muscle, then sew up the wound when it's clean, and continue the treatment until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	And for the larger blisters, hang them.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	No matter in which parts of the body or anywhere else, this is a disease that is named "fungus" due to its appearance, and it has a delicate root, and large heads;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are some small ones and many large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw two homes who had them in their stomachs that resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no distinction, they were white, had a small root, and split open, and within they corroded due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I copied them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces in the other six. The organs at the incision are such that when you look they see that the flesh is moist, and the appearance of the inside is white and wet with a delicate root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If you seize the broad spot, and have the fire cautery present.

quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil burns
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	Its appearance comes from the cautery of wounds or fissures in syphilis, and is on the belly; there are some ulcers like this, as happens with other cuts, or bleeding from veins or arteries according to what has come before, or from windiness.

si est eclites soulement;	if it is merely minor;

de la circoncision	of circumcision
