puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment of ointments until he is well.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion has reached the bone, you must remove it and scrape thoroughly, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see that the tooth is rotten, remove it from both jaws as was explained earlier, then treat until he is well.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is severe and hurts greatly, you must remove it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail near the thymus in a crosswise manner, and be careful that the cut does not go down to the flesh under the nail, for it would cause too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, place something above which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain is originating from the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	I must adjust what is born in the hands of some people by chance and has thick flesh, and by chance it may have bones or there's none at all times, and often there isn't a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is within any of us.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those born without any defect do not move, and those born with a defect at the joint, by chance, do move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of one who is muscular appears light, in such manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it down to the root of a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those born at the root of the joint require treatment:
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold it with copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the rear joint, it is necessary that you first handle until you reach the round flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable tool according to this, and then treat until it is clean.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The decisions that come together at the elbow arise from birth, or from an injury to a wound, or from the application of fire, or from similar actions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you solder that joint, so that it should be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two damp cloths or sponges soaked in oil rosin, so they do not weld together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two thin pieces of beeswax, until they are joined together, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When we perform soldering with her palm, if she applies the soldering paste as it should be done.
des vils	of the villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	These are thick veins filled with numerous melancholic superfluities that come from multiple members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more comes in legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So you must give them once purging of bile, and then heal them from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One method involves bleeding, and the other results in black blood being discharged;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The other method is to open the vein and force it completely out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision is done in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First apply hot water to the leg vigorously until the large artery is weakened. Then hold the leg steady near the skin above the knee down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein near my location, or in II or III, with a broad size, then elevate and press with your hand for the black blood, from one end to the other, until as much blood flows out as the virtues of the malady can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	Then let it heal, and instruct them to dip in meat juices that darken this blackness.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And resume the evacuation and cleaning whenever the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The method of treatment is as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Warm the leg from the affected area, if there is hair present, then immerse it in water, and raise the leg in hot water until it turns red, and expand the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have a cautery tool, heat it on the fire, and then apply it directly to the vein along its entire length from near the neck down to the knee joint, or in the area below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then cut into the flesh with an awl, and scorch each side of the vein until you see it when you touch it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And it appears red and black, and when it enters the leather, it seems like a white thread;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then pull out the wire until it is raised above the skin, and then cut into the flesh gently with an awl, then apply it to another part three times in succession;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scorch the skin above the vein until you see it, then lift it with the rod as you did before, and cut into another awl, in the same way as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then fit another size, or more if needed, then lift it, and fit to the foot of the pie, then guide and lift until the second size fits.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then stretch it gradually from size to size, until all strength remains, then fit it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot stretch and lift it, insert a pin through the entire thick thread, and bind and guide it, and if there's not enough of it, turn your hand from side to side until there's enough.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure it doesn't bind up, for if it binds up, one can neither stretch nor lift it, and this is harmful to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you've stretched it all, place wet wool in the wound covered with wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat him while he is still healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the limb is twisted and turned into a bundle together, and it's not straight, as we have said, then you must cut through forcefully but do not bend it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And guide it as we have explained before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	It should be shaped like the iron when one cuts with a tool, and you should not slice, so as not to cut through the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it should be thickly curved; if it were too fine, it would cut through the vein, but make it thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein runs under the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil without moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And by chance it may be born in another place than in legs, and this happens due to corruption that comes from under the skin, if it comes inside the body as snakes and worms do, piercing between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein so are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then change the blood, and it begins the vein to exit outwards, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When you open the joints, it is necessary that you wrap around with a piece of leather half way up to two and a half yards., then tie it off, and leave the leather hanging on the leg, and every time there is a little left exposed, if you wrap around inside the leather, and tie it off.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off some part and wrap again by pulling up the remaining piece, but do not cut to its root until all of it has come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut too much, it goes into the flesh and brings about pus and decay at that spot, causing a harmful illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For which reason it is necessary that she be treated gradually and little by little until completion, and that she not leave anything or more than usual.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And in this case concerning the vein when it is treated with long palm lengths or ten palms, and one person came to me, whose vein was X palms long and attached from that position. And when you grasp it, if it yields after one or two pulls, and piercing until depth ensures all releases;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And remove the substance within and apply internal remedies to prevent corruption every day, then treat it as for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And with this vein, use dry hands, and likewise when it opens at the ankle or foot joint, or when it comes from pulling too much, and without wetting.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat accordingly as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it has appeared many times on cows, and it's a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body going up and down, causing one to feel well at each limb, until it reaches the skin where it was heading, then it jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is riddled with putrefaction from various fluids, such as when they come towards worms and snakes and roundworms or hookworms in the stomach;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And there is confusion about its nature, for when it travels through the body and ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, by chance it returns and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and milked, if one cannot expect anything until it is about to:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore, you should bind the head tightly above and below with a strong bandage, then proceed to milk it, and if it does not drain properly into the flesh, and you cannot find it, then apply heat cautery to it while milking, until it drains;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest troubles it causes, if they flow through the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it approaching or near the eye, then bind tightly over it with a piece of wood, then proceed to milk it and force it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	It is necessary to use the remedy for cleansing sores of medicinal solutions for the removal of body fluids, and it is important to prevent the spoilage of meats from becoming putrid.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called in our land 'vakirir', and it is a pain that comes to any limbs, and when it leaves one limb, it moves to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to help a sick woman, and she showed me her arms, revealing a small swelling in the vein of one arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, it rose as if a worm was climbing her shoulder, faster than anything else, like molten silver when cut from one thing to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain left that arm and penetrated her shoulder, and then shortly afterwards spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was twisting inside her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how it moved from member to member in such a way, for I had never seen this disease in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	In every way, I wanted many that well had wanted to move pain of themselves to another, but I did not want it myself, as I see in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had a naked belly and her veins exposed, and for this reason that the constriction of wind became apparent;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they don't become evident according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have wet bodies and their veins enclosed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, open it from above and below quickly, and then proceed with care until that constriction of wind in the body releases.
et cauterize le leu;	And apply cautery to the affected area;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And if you don't see it at your eyes, seek the remedy for those who relieve wind troubles, such as stinking pills, snake venom pills, and similar other remedies.
des saiettes	The phrase "des saiettes" refers to arrows or projectiles that may be embedded in wounds. It is often used in medical texts of the medieval period when describing treatments for injuries caused by projectiles, such as those sustained from battles or hunting accidents.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of their sizes is such that some have large points, and small ones, and those with hair, and soldered ones;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and there are those that have two angles, and those with tongues, and among some there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and there is the one that urinates in no member but does so in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the main body part, such as the brain, heart, liver, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it urinates, then in no part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you must perform the extraction of this arrow, for death comes later in various conditions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear and the arrow is not fully removed, you should extract it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces and hits bone, and starts a fluid leak coming from under the head, is when there is paralysis, stiffness, inversion, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms with confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps it stops fluid from flowing out through the nose or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And sometimes it affects speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And from the moist wound, white pus resembling hairs seems to come out, and also like ashes of burnt flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And when you notice this sign, take care with the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it hasn't been removed.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow is when it bleeds or stops bleeding; it indicates that it's close to the left nipple and feels like it might have been stuck in something hard rather than empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance, if the arrow stops bleeding like hair and black blood comes out, and brings on coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	So, without doubt, it means that the person will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never lets out pus is when there's no foam bursting from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with a cold chill.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow bleeds in the undercoat of the buttocks, it indicates that it is behind the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	And causes great pain and great suffering and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And it moves the entire limb from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach is hit, by chance if there's any undigested flesh from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach is hit, and there's no meat passing through the intestines in the jump, then there's no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow is inside the bladder, and urine spurts out and goes outside, and the patient feels intense pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, forearm, back, thigh, leg, and similar limbs, are safe depending on various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is within your nerve or artery, and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because that's how you should handle such a situation.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one person who was hit by an arrow near the nose in its root:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and removed it from the other side of the ear's grease, and it was completely well.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And tried to extract an arrow that had fallen into the ear's grease near the membrane and bone, the arrow was recovered, and one could not reach more than its tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow's string, all without hurting his ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The body healed well, and no harmful incidents befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was the Arabic one for ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I pulled out the arrows, and skillfully removed them as I pulled, making the Christian heal well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And extracted an arrow from a house, where it was stuck in the stomach, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after passing 30 days, if his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, set it free, and pulled forcefully; there was no adverse incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find an arrow has fallen on the back of a house, and the wound healed tightly there;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And the arrow stays within, not finding relief from its natural functions or experiencing harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, who was struck by an arrow in his face, and the wound was sealed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and thus he endured without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and no other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And once an arrow was shot at the king in his palace home, he was caught in the midst of a battle, and was slightly leaning towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow had fully entered him.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was summoned for treatment after it had been three days since he was hit.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be greatly constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I wanted to test its subtlety thoroughly, but I could not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was pain and discomfort traveling across his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put on him a poultice that is adhesive and digestive; because his ears were not inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and it showed me that the ear of the arrow was visible.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the poultice every day and cured the wound immediately. He then stayed with the patient for a long time until he felt the arrow inside his nose;
et il le me dist.	and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive ague medicine to the wound for several days until it opened, and then I tested it, feeling the tip of the arrow that was lodging in his ear;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then adjust during the opening of the wound through that blood-repelling medicine, until the head of the arrow appears visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and puncture well the ends for three months, and then loosen so that the wound heals to a point where I clip with my forceps, from both sides, and it could not escape;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	thus I did not cease to refine and invent methods for tools, until I had one day with properly made forceps, according to what the shape will come at the end of this chapter, whether I use them, and leave the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	thus I did so, and healed the wound, and completely cured the patient.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	You should know the quality of extracting certain arrows, so you place your treatment upon what I do not specify, because books cannot contain all knowledge.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but among wise masters and colleagues you will find some more precise knowledge, concerning both what is available and lacking in current practice. Discover nine new works, and nine tools for the discharge of extraneous matters that occur within this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I state that arrows are embedded in limbs according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either by the way they enter or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	The case where the arrow enters through the flesh or where it is inserted, it penetrates into the muscle, and this has happened without any exceptions so far.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump now, let it grow until the flesh is thoroughly cooked inside, and achieve its release.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it's stuck in the bone and cannot be released, let it stay like that for some days, and remove a little each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Then it will jump; if it doesn't jump, drill inside through all the subtle woods until the interior muscles are widened, and then guide it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and reaches up to one of the lungs near the brain, or any of the incidents I've described happens before the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if you don't remove it, but let it grow until it's even after a few days; because if the arrow reaches up to there, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and not to its full depth, and does not pierce any organ, causing no harm for days without a bad event, then the removal device for extraction should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is so deeply inserted and cannot come out at all, then you should administer hot rods internally, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has returned inside the body so you cannot see it, then search for it thoroughly.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then guide it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot find it due to the tightness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then probe as far as the wound allows.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And if you can guide the arrow, pull it out. If there are ears attached to where she holds the arrow, extract any bone that is stuck halfway between two and your reach limit, then break or bend the ears of the arrow as far as possible until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And very carefully ensure you do not break the arrow, but pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't achieve it in one go, until the arrow reaches your hand, let it get stuck there, then pull it out because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding during surgery opposes you, then apply what we have instructed about treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of incisions near nerves and veins, and do your best to carefully remove the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and guide the patient according to the form they were in before the arrow fell, for this is the greatest aid that it should be possible, and if you cannot do so, then place them according to what the symptoms show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that came from another direction, or if there is no sign of it anywhere, or if the skin is swollen in some place quite obviously:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Therefore raise up, as long as the tongs can take hold, and then restrain:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held within the bone, turn your hand around, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then guide it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot come out, leave her still and then restart the extraction until she jumps out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is inside him, thrust it all the way through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is stuck and you see that the instrument needs to be applied, if you apply the instrument correctly, so that the arrowhead enters the hair of the tool;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then thrust forcefully, and if the arrow is embedded, you apply the instrument at its pointed entry to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has struck him, then it is necessary for you to remove all the tissue around where I am entering or have entered, if possible, and then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is stuck or in pain or in the abdomen or bladder or ribs and it's close to the vital organs, and you can't see clearly, then cover yourself up, and you do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And protect against covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound; that is a task you should undertake.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows resemble bird beaks, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And in many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is similar to the feathers of a bird, for it points at the tip of the arrow, as this shape illustrates:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape for pressing and holding, as shown here, is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	The veins from which we bleed are thirty-one, out of which there are sixteen at the head, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two smaller ones located behind the ears, which are called "the two 'herbaches'";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries in the two visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two upper parts of the eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	And the vein that is found at the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that's located above the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two jugulars which are in the collarbone area;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins that are located above in the cheeks of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augueherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins we usually know consist of five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it's under the left rib, and they call this "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the median is called "fast", and it's made up of the cephalic and the basilic veins, and they call this "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the rib is either on the left or in the right side, and they call it by the common folk "lung of the belly", and it's under the ribs, and that’s where the heart lies, which opens clearly above the stomach.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the artery is the vein that's located between the index and ring fingers, and it has two loops;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and at the ankle there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is near the curve of the belly on the left side of the rib, and the second one at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nose", which is in the ankle of the other rib side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins beside those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The treatment of veins that are behind the ears helps with the cauterization of old patients, and aids in migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of the surgeon, as I've explained, and that you warm the head of the patient, rubbing the area where the veins or arteries are located with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then pinch the base of the neck until you can see both veins behind the ears on either side of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Place your hand there, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, let it guide you;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and place it just below the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand to right above the entire length of the vein, cut through the skin and the vein up to the bone well, allowing blood to flow out as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then apply pressure and secure it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have spoken about the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The health of the second arteries that are in the two temples, if they are ancient and hardened, and those who have accustomed to eye drops, and on the chest of feverish tears by the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of this surgeon is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And when the patient's throat is squeezed until both arteries can be clearly seen;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And feel under your finger, and then indicate on the right side;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then gently place your hand over the artery at your right index, and hold the scalpel under it, then gently lift the artery up top, and cut it, just like you did with the other arteries, and let out the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your hand on the vein for an hour, then place it on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and when the wound heals, leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken about them and their extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the forehead vein is as important as the healing of the frontal artery in old diseases, and for migraine, and heat.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is that the patient twists its neck in pain until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool called 'digester', whose shape is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, and allow blood to flow according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then free the patient from the neck, and tie the artery as long as it remains healthy and there is no cut to an open flame wide.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Otherwise, it's not good for the flames to be too strong;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And the wound should be across rather than straight, because the bone is nearby, and by chance, the flames might break when they are fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps with them, and at the nose, and at the cheek, and in the ear by the ear canal, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is that the patient twists their neck to tighten a certain bandage, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and make the cut into the healthy part, a little across, one length of a flame's width slightly larger. For there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they might break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make sure to drain the blood as much as needed, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The treatment of the vein opening near the nose is valued for fever, and for clear mucus, and for diseases affecting the face, such as migraine and swelling that comes to the face, and also when it's old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of this treatment is that the patient tenses their neck and holds their left nose to your left hand, take a thin flame lengthwise, and stick it in between the two nostrils into the gap where the vein isn't opening well, as the vein doesn't open properly there, and blood collection will now begin.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not push too deeply inside, and make the incision according to your need, then let it rest for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is in the form of flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The hygiene of the two intestines aids in tightening the gallbladder, and at the beginning of mingling diseases, and for many illnesses, and in putrefaction, and corrosion, and in herpes, and indigestions;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of hygiene is such that the patient tightens their throat from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the surgeons be on top of the patient's head, and the patients sit at the edge, then apply hygiene across a broad but somewhat narrow length, then draw out the blood moderately or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then restart by making another incision on the other vein, then untie the knot, and hold both veins slightly tightly, so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The care of veins in the mouth aids in their condition, and it deals with gum decay, cracks on lips, nosebleeds, and inner cheeks.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing is to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left. You can identify them by their black color, and because they have small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Then tie both of them. If you do not know which to tie and are in doubt, tie the larger one from each side. And treat both veins above and below them in the same way, because it's the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of healing beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of veins that are below the tongue requires assistance after the healing of the cephalic area, and this is at the constriction of the throat, and for eye diseases, and for mouth ailments;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the surgeon is such that when your hands are between them before the sun, and you lift the tongue, and look down on each side you find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore heal both of them, but do not go too deep, for they are near the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly treated are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	One method is by piercing with all the fire of a broad meridian flame, or with a subtle olive one if it's like a cutting knife, and this is called "aneusil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are broad and fine according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame dart is quite famous and very wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it requires to open the full, bloody veins filled with evident blood, and which contain thick blood and turbidity;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that's like the shape of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more slender and pointed, and used for clarifying subtle veins, or it has subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The purification of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that occur in the throat, and neck, and stomach, and abdomen;

et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And it must not be held by fire, but cut like a hare.

elle apert manifestement;	it clearly opens;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut it with the fire like a hare, as we have said.

Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulging up as high as the urine of a child, and if the wound is red and subtle, know that it is from an artery:

et estainche li sans.	And stop the bleeding.

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of healing depends on your thought process.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you need to know about hygiene is that hygiene is practiced solely for maintaining health and preventing future illnesses;

et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, heal her in all the ways you can, and by crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it's better if you touch her, because the limbs are without pain, and she responds well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you cannot find it, heal no part of what opens or behind the foot, and towards the small toe, and guard against nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And make such corrections to the blood that you see, and then release the knot, and put on cotton and tighten it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction healings
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuum cups are made from horns, or spiders, or worms;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is done according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by causing blood to come out and then attracting it away, or alternatively without causing blood to come out.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping done by causing bleeding follows two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it can be done instantly, or without using fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping done by causing bleeding and extraction of blood is performed over the four corners of the body, from which one is entirely made of bone;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other ones are around the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the other two on the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction cup under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction cup over the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup over the pimples;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction cups on both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction cups on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and suction therapy does not deal with blood, rather it's for small veins that are scattered in the body, and because of this it doesn't weaken you at all, just as we do with vein health;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not right for it to be administered without fire or in any illness that comes from overfullness, until all the bodies are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if suction is needed for diseases or by habit, if we do it every hour at the beginning of each month, or at the end, and throughout and in every phase;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they have need to suction, if they weigh too much initially;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for those who find congestion and redness in their face, and head, and neck, and there is cloudiness around the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and spit out blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and for those who tremble, and see through cloudy blood and veined skin and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially during the last month before giving birth, we instruct to breathe after three hours each day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The cure of the mouth helps in the relief of inflammation in the head ... affecting the eyes, and it should not be that it comes after the elimination of all over the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this practice of blowing air is in the field of hygiene for the head, and it should not be used by those who have a cold constitution, or who suffer from dyspepsia, because doing so causes great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And it should not be used by someone who practices watchfulness, or who has cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often gets relieved from it, becomes oblivious, and because of this one must place the suction cup somewhat further down due to the confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Blowing into the neck is in the field of hygiene for the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason it is useful for squeezing the heel, and making incisions into the channel of the heart, and for everything else, and for fullness;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is better to do this with restraint, because if you hold too tightly, it can lead to impairment or indigestion and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The practices of blowing into the second ribs of the neck are useful for relieving head pains, eye infections and toothaches, and also effective in cases of stridor, and pain at the root of teeth, and they fall under the field of hygiene of the basilic vein.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand when placing it, not to touch the artery, and not to observe any breaks in blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation of the area under the chin is worth to disease of the mouth, and decay of gums, as well as other illnesses that occur in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it's part of the health of the inner lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the shoulders comes from diseases caused by heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Ventilation of the armpits is as important as three veins in the arms, for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply because the chest is naked of flesh and contains organs and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The suction cup placed on the back is worth to bleeding disorders in the abdomen and diseases nearby; it must be large and made of wood or bamboo for better treatment.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perchance, if she were subtle, she would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The suction cups on the legs are applied directly because they draw blood from all over the body, and help with old pain in the kidneys, bladder, and lower back, also relieving swellings;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	They are in the locations of the two shins and the two ankles, and overall they weaken the body after long use, and cause fatigue in multiple conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you first place it empty and apply pressure steadily, then move it quickly and evenly, never stopping this action until you see the area turn red and swell, and observe the reddening due to blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then apply fire, and reattach the suction cups, and take care in the positioning of the horns, for there are those with thick flesh, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is necessary to cut only once, and it is proper to make large wounds, and somewhat deeper ones.
et suce legierement.	And suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the one without is large, it may be necessary to cut twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time for the subtle removal of a larger vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is very thick without, it may be necessary to cut the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	When we wish to drain little by little from the blood, we only pierce once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much of the blood, then we often reapply;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the bone is expected, so firmly hammered, and the ends are such that the joints are pierced suddenly, it fits for those with thick skin and firm flesh, who have been long troubled, that you apply the nostrums of suck bulbs where an opening and disassembling appear:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it's in this blue state, or from sweet almond oil, or from pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it's yellow, from mustard oil, or from lily, or from chamomile, or other similar substances.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of melilot, or turpentine, or oil of nutmeg, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to be treated has thick flesh and large abrasions, it is not suitable to apply oil at all, but after leeching with pink water, or cold water, or water from a rose, or water from a pumpkin, or water from porcelain, or other similar substances, you should wash them.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And to those who have much moisture, if they rise from sweat, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with excesses ascend from old wine, or from urine water, or from decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar substances.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not appropriate to use suction cups before or during the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep after suction, it is necessary that he be aware, when he should be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch over those who are being cured and are choleric, and if the patient is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It is necessary for them to eat cold things, such as pomegranates, endive and lettuce, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	Eat eels, and pork, and meat with moisture.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with cold constitutions, they should drink honey syrup and fragrant half-aged wine, which is between old and new, eat some porridge, eat eels and small birds and chicks;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day they will be suctioned, they should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no one meat or garlic or mustard before or after ventilation, in order to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And sieve the flour but it is not fitting that which is hot should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are placed to cause irritation are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and in gout, and on the belly and womb and kidneys and hip. But this member does not tolerate being irritated by heat, and one should do it forcefully only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we do with nipples when the child fails to suck.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	in order to thin the viscosity in the limb, as we apply suction cups on the belly and womb to reduce its thickness.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And for pain when there is an obstruction or stone, if it is attracted by its adhesive power to such obstructions, or if it empties the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus she does it when one puts her on the liver and on the stomach when there is retained wind, and these suction cups are applied empty for to expel wind alone;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in the case of pleurisy diseases, and in such manner one fills the suction cup with hot water or with water that has boiled herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has II inches and a half in length from the tip, and at its middle third it is about as wide as one's finger, just like to insert an awl, and made of iron or steel so that it does not irritate the patient upon being placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And there is in the middle a rod across of an arachnid or iron, for to put a torch in possession, and it is used whether large or small according to illnesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suckling bottles for children are different from those for adults, and those for skinny individuals are different from those for fatty ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must place this suction cup thus on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the wax candle or the heated rod, and insert it through the suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the suction cup to avoid burning the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and you should do so at the point we have mentioned, so that when one wants to, if there is vapor going off, and remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And follow the same line as before, and repeat often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Therefore, when it comes to the suction cup which is administered in pleuresin disease, during all types of colds, there should not be any pus or impurities; and it is only used fully once it is filled with coldness, then placed only on the body part.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Only suction cups are used in limbs where one cannot place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their naked places of scars, such as elbows or knees, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of their application is that when you find suction cups that are in mild coldness without pus, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And place them in mild water, until they are familiar, with no bulges in their abdomens;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cure with bloodletting and suction cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place it on the sores;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and weep, if there is a spot where suction cups can be placed, put them there, because this yields little later.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the arm then dip it in water well, and then incise;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if it heals too quickly due to the effect of suction cups, moisturize with a linen cloth dipped in cold water, and place it there, until the suction cup wounds turn red;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wounds are multiplied, then place powdered vitriol or garlic, and similar items, until they become stenchy;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you place half the peeled hazelnuts inside the wound, and leave them until they heat up within, it will now stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the veins are not to be found elsewhere, rub with fresh blood-soaked material, or you insert a needle until blood flows from it and then place it. Once they start smelling the blood, they will heat up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they sweat, then powder a little aloes and ground grain, or ashes, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fracture and alleviation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that these matters of this chapter, they were not seen in any old books, nor did anyone read about them;
