et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the knowledge has been lost in our land, because I have never found anyone who was good at it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, because through the knowledge of old books, which I have studied so much that I have dealt with this science, and by experimentation, and through the experience of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained within it, and summarized at the end, clearly showing the forms of the instruments used, as I did in these two chapters previously.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we outline or introduce this book's main points and chapters where the wise people use their understanding, and remain faithful to truth. Let those who have experienced this know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twists or pain occur in any part, it is necessary to quickly treat the patient from both sides, without letting anything prevent you, such as weakness, children, or elderly people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If the place you're tightening is too tight, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and use cold joints, which means cold meats, and oyster flesh and venison, do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and let the body not be too full of meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt about an abscess or spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient's body has adapted to its usual government as it was using it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with foods that cause a heavy digestion or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and nuts, and pies, and beef stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at times, after an operation, it can move again more quickly than the breaking.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones in old and weak individuals cannot be properly healed or sutured according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too soft, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But if there is no remedy, reset it on the broken bone and large thorns that stick out. Join the limb together as tightly as before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not finish his work entirely, and for this reason he should be nourished with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from the fracture of the heel, or of the leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others through cutting, such as the length of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a fracture with injury, or a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every way has his own device and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to his mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the breaking of the bone is known by that his hand hurts and opens well outward, and feels a press on it;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist or soreness in the hand, and the body does not feel great pain, if there is no breakage;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may well have twisting, or cracking, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But do not move it with your hand yourself, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	Know that the break occurring in the journey, and where it splits into two parts, they should now place them evenly, just like when placing an abscess on its side.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if it's a hard abscess that comes to the surface, so he lets no day pass until the abscess is alleviated;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then place it evenly until you can do so lightly and skillfully. Know that the restoration of this is easier than those with pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then tighten it, as it should be done hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it's split into two parts, whether they are hands or feet, or at your hand if they're small limbs, or if they are divided by two cords, or one cord and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the injured parts of the limb are healed, you adjust it with every effort using additions in their respective places as much as you can, and be sure to avoid causing injury or pain through your actions to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And test it thoroughly with your hand if you feel it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it is correctly aligned, do not overstretch or apply too much pressure. Do this gently as those who remove the abscess by their own efforts use heat and muscle contractions on the limb, as we have wished many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are in place, ensure you take good care of the patient so they do not move them, whether awake or asleep, walking or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, this is not enough; it must be placed in such a position that he does not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And see to it that it is put straight, so there is no distortion when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb should be according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied by size and extent and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are smaller limbs, such as arms and legs, and others like them:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	They should be wrapped in soft, fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are larger, such as thighs and calves:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	They should be wrapped in a broad and firm bandage, for wide bands encircle the entire large limb, restraining it evenly from all sides, so that there is no awkwardness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lightly apply the ointment for three rounds or four according to the limb, and hold your hand somewhat tightly throughout this process. Then move upwards beyond the breakage point and hold less tightness; allowing the breakage to move a little away from the breakage area.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the area gradually and gradually, until you reach a substantial part of his healthy side, then take up another connection, and return back to where you began near the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the area around the breakage point, and hold it moderately, neither too hard nor too soft, just as we explained in the first round above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place the linen or cloth bands between the applied ointments until it's all evenly spread, then secure everything with a bandage. Lastly, position your well-made stars on top; if there is no pus or swelling present.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then apply something soothing for the abscess, and which alleviates the swelling, and leaves it in this state for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then stretch over your ears, and let them be half the width of a hair tightly, or from a shaft that is used for making arrows, or from palm leaves, and they should fit according to this pattern:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	However, it is necessary that the ears placed on the gap be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let them also be as long as is suitable for limbs of smallness or largeness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then stretch over the ears in the same way you did with the first attempt, then tie a supplementary thread on top, just like you did above the break in the first instance;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	More constriction occurs there, as before, at this point.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and be soft like linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as in works of the folks who make their looped knots with linen cords twisted, and that's great error, because the knot can't be uniform if it's too fine, and it doesn't suit to have less than half a thumb's width between each pair of threads.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are irritated by the edges of the stitches after tightening during their healing, then place linen patches or raveled wool on them, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is inflamed and the ribs are broken, I will then describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to hold back too much of your efforts when healing broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it's not suitable to place these loops until after five days or seven, or more depending on your tolerance of pus that comes each time a new one occurs;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the method of ancient plastering to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And it is that you take some flour which stands by the walls of the mill, and mix this with plenty of eggs, and prepare this concoction neither too thin nor too thick, then use it, and this is the common method for plastering to restore fractures in various positions, just as much for women and small children, because there is no matter whether it's too expensive or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method for plastering that restores fractures, dislocations and torsions:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take ginger, garlic, nutmeg, and asafetida, and gum Arabic, add water to make X parts.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mint and aloe vera, make up for V parts.
alechil VIIII З.;	Allium (garlic) VIIIX parts.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make powder, and mix it with beaten egg yolk;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If their body heat is hot, they should use this plaster, because it has a good composition and quickly heals broken bones, being beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of applying plaster that is useful for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take meat and vinegar, add X parts of salt;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Myrrh and aloes, add nine parts of them;
acaice VI З.;	Add six parts of acacia;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Add ten parts of Armenian balm, grind well, mix with water or beaten egg yolk, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method for applying plaster to dislocated joints and broken bones, it eases the pain coming on, and when they use the bone, it breaks the swelling:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new lamb, and cook its milk with ease and oil, and place it under your head.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Bandages do not heal completely, but they are better for soothing abscesses, and properly treating the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of plastering which restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poplar leaves, grind them together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster is for the restoration of bone fracture and to relieve the removal of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of valerian, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour from rice, from each take a part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind it, mix it with wine, and when the limbs are warmed, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plastering more forcibly than the first, when pus is returning to the recovery of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take the roots of valerian, and sesame seeds, balsam, melilot, and sorrel, and flowers of violets and chamomile, from all take a part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that only beeswax ointment made of wax and oil should be applied to the broken limb for restoration without anything else. He states that it must not be too soft or too hard but just right.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, substances slightly heated and somewhat dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of plastering that is useful for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take the brains and feathers of cooked men or bird feathers, and liverworts, and woodlice, and earth equal in quantity, grind them together, make a plaster from it, and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then apply the plaster slightly later, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is their bone moved out of its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If you do not apply the plaster with your hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itchiness, without rest or swelling, then you should act quickly, remove the plaster, and apply the plaster anew;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	Take a light cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and dip it in water, then remove the moisture, until the itching stops and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, moistened in water or oil, and secure it with a belt until you are sure of removing any pus;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	Let the inflammation and pain in the limb subside, then relieve the pain, then continue with gentle manipulation, and a little plaster, but do not strain it as strongly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus is coming out and the area is red, painful, swollen and oozing, indicating inflammation throughout, then you will need to apply plaster and bind it, start again as you did initially, in exactly the same way.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the limb that we have said, or if it is not released only after three, four, or five days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And never let it go for more than XX days, as we see, until the fracture heals and brings about alignment of the bone above;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Therefore keep it restrained longer than at first, and strengthen its flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see that the bone is healing better than necessary, know that no remedies can come about;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Let the bone then be immersed in hot water, every time you untie it, and let that happen every third day, and clean a little of the wound;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this process then cut out the remedies from the limb, and quickly heal whatever the foolish eye sees that leaves the limb deformed:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is bad, and there are difficulties with it, and I don't see anything else but leaving it and opening it straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Regarding various methods of breaking bones
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because there are fractures that result from the impact of a sword, and in these cases, the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the symphysis which is at the end of the bone, like in the case of a mallet or staff.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this reason, this type of fracture is called "mallet injury".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword hits the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And these two types of fractures have large or small injuries.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack, or fracture of the stone collarbone, or under the stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture partly through, which approaches until it reaches the membrane beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound may be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has healed within the bone as delicate as a hair, and has small cracks, and because of this it is called this breakage "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if there is a wound made or caused by striking with stone, or falling, or from something seemingly trivial, and it causes the part of the bone to enter the body, so that they are together as hammers would be when struck upon hammers;
si entre li piere dedens.	if within the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have wet bones below, like in children's bones;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	It occurs in all these ways of breakage where small fragments are lost, like with maggots.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all methods of breaking through the diminution upon them, and the examination by touch, and through the corrupt flesh that is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs inside it, if the breakage shows black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a breakage, beware of any bad accidents due to illness, if you see no harmful incident, such as vomiting bile, loss of intellect, extension and rigidity, fever ague, and if the eyes emerge and turn red, or show other similar symptoms in various conditions, you cannot be certain of recovery.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a terrible accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nose comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in winter, you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day after the month; so that when the pus around the bone becomes infected, and accidents as we said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the breaking of the bone reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary for you to cut the broken part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you apply the hot tip of a needle to the raw flesh and expose as much bone as possible in all ways that you can, and at the shape of the wound more than you can, and if blood flow comes with the exposure of the bone, or pus appears, use what is necessary, and when you fill the gap with wet bandages soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the pus subsides, and ensure there is no blood flow;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin digging into the bone, and this is done according to two methods of operation:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is that you cut close to the front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut that is larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others broad, they should be pointed, and made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and perform the operation lightly so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is outside and hard, it must be pierced through internally, in such a way that cuts are made with thimbles, not all the way through so as not to pierce beyond the bone when tested, and there should be a margin or circle above the point, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it must be that you have several of them, so that each returns to its place relative to the thickness of the bone, so that you have thimbles for all tests;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three ways of cauteries:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality to pierce through the broken bone is that you place the cautery on the bone and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then place the cautery elsewhere a little later, and do this all around. Then cut into the space of the bone that is between the teeth, doing so more subtly than you can, gently, just like we said, until you bring the bone to your hand or to any tool you have such as forceps;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And make sure not to touch the brain or the pituitary gland.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, if necessary, resaw what was left of the bone with all another instrument like a tooth. But it should be sturdier and more delicate than the other tooth;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if there remains no little bones, nor any scales, if you gently shake them with your tools;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then cleanse the wound of the bandages and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way to treat wounds is as Galen said, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he uses strong ligation, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, it is necessary to uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the fracture opens and moves, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision, from which its shape is given:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side only, and divide the flesh into two parts, so that your cut is facing towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike with a small hammer on it, so that you gently crush the entire bone, and be well aware of the wound material that is nearby.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it opens to the bone, gently crush it, for the bone is well sensitive without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture doesn't penetrate just to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, with small pieces present, then after that abrasiveness, and remove the scales with a subtle razor you must have in various quantities, for administering the most suitable one to each area according to the treatise and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are in front of large razors, and after even finer ones, and never cease doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each other type of hair cutting and delicate breaking, you must adapt according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be answered by the one who has devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the scab is discovered, it is necessary that you apply a linen bandage according to the size of the wound, and soak with rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another bandage doubled in two or three layers, and soak it with wine and rose oil, and place it on the first bandage;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this as lightly as you can so that it does not weigh down the scab; then apply another bandage over it without pulling too hard that only the wound touches.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And let it do so for one or two days, until the abscess has subsided, then release them, and administer medications such as roots of this herb, meal of garlic, incense powder, and myrrh, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And from these things make powder, put it on the wound, and administer those medications locally without causing irritation;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And see that the wound is kept clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor let it become too swollen; because when swelling assembles under the skin tissue, it can move and constrict, causing great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And when one applies something sharp there, it cuts through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then be careful therefore, if no accidents come to the patient as we have said, there is doubt without fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no fear comes from that which we have applied, assuming it has this virtue, then you should take a portion of honey, and three parts of goose oil and one spoonful of glue, and spread them on the affected area;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the appropriate healing method until it is sound.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that twice the parts above the nose are broken, or only one part by itself, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And that area is made of cartilage and does not break, nor allow bending or twisting forces, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should bend your little finger or to the inside of the nose, and place an equal break within your index finger, and outwardly through the nostril, until the nose regains its natural form.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose and cannot come to the nostrils, it must be that you put it level with the tip of a hair a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, redo the operation, and strive to restore on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or the eighth day, when the abscess is dressed and calmed, then apply to the nose tip with a poultice of linen bandage, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you may crush it from another side, if the break is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let them be as large as they fill out the cavities of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer thinks to moisten the warts with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I don't think it's quite right, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a mixture of egg whites and powder from grinding;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent, until the bone is strong, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And do not use any goose feathers or ointments instead of tents, and if there's wind resistance, and the air stays stagnant, causing the patient to feel it among them;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	just do whatever you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out through the nose as you work on it, then apply a wet cloth or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a little pot of almond oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not come out, apply a plaster to the outside, made from ground frankincense and incense powder mixed with yolk of egg, then place it on light bandages and don't bind it tightly around the neck;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the rupture is small near the neck and broken into small pieces, use tools suitable for this task, then clean the wound from infected matter and sew it up, using plasters and ointments suitable for that purpose;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the nose, then you treat it with remedies, and I place cloths soaked in vinegar, as long as it remains healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured and there is no wound on the surface, and only the breakage is external, not at all broken into two halves but rather split internally throughout, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the breakage is in the right part, that you bend your second finger on the inside of the knee;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the breakage is in the left jawbone, then bend your second finger of the right hand and gently push the break inward, and do it with the other hand from behind, and place them evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is divided into two parts, then it is necessary to provide extension for both halves, ensuring they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And when tooth movements or rupture occur, stretch them with a gold thread or silver or silk thread, then place a wax on the broken jawbone, and place two layers of cloth on top.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the cloth a well-made large slab or a piece of leather of equal size, long and wide according to the jawbone, and fasten it at several points with strings that you can find. Instruct the patient to rest and consume light meat portions.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you notice the figure changing, dislocate it on the third day, then reset whatever has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and place them on top, using ground powder mixed with plenty of egg or saffron flour, after you have removed the wax.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place on the plaster a light cloth, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, leave them until they are healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times, it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And when pus comes out during an incision, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there's both breakage and injury together, remove any part of the bone that has been broken.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if it is necessary to use instruments suitable for this task during the operation.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains nothing, if the wound is wide, place one plaster suitable for it over it to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	By the power of
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forces break many times before, towards the shoulder, and breaking is according to three methods:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or it breaks and dries out in two parts, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is breaking with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the operations are like when breaking occurs with injury, that you have two helpers, so that one slices off the shoulder where the strength breaks;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends along the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then place the break evenly on your hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there's neither appearance nor distortion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, then place a round sponge under the shoulder for the patient, of cloth or wool, and make it as large as your need dictates;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And they reduce it gently, restraining the spear with your hand, so that you make an even break, as is fitting.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force outwards due to it coming forward, so that the patient lies on their back, and places a half pillow under their shoulder, and pushes the shoulder blade downwards, until the bone of the force is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And direct the crack to your fingers, and if you find splinters, it's right that you split them;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	And pull out the fragments gently, and if the bone cannot join by any pressure, then cut to one of the incisions you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but when you apply force to this tool, it helps to push out fluids:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and seems like a spoon, not completely inside, and be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the operation;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, just like the cut of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of the removal of pus, if you clean the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt about removing pus, then dress the wound with bandages and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pus comes out, if moisture arrives, apply oil roses and vinegar and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The grinding of the bone, when it concerns wounds and surgery, is to place on the bone a plaster made from the powder of the mill and some yolk of egg, and put light wads underneath, and apply a splint over it, if you need to.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very long band about the size of a palm in width, then place two layers of bandage over the wads, and apply plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a strip of about three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the bandage, such that only the edge of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And set the candle near the burn, and turn the bandage up to the neck, and over the healthy elbow, and over the diseased elbow;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And reset each part; and when you see that the candle's heat supports the wound growth, and you clearly see that the wax does not move over the fractured bone, then reward each day, and when it's removed, keep it restrained.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And let the diseased substance drain on his back, and place him with a small pillow under the elbow to lift the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	So ease the strain of the muscles by aligning the shoulder; or you tie his arm to the neck, and don't untie until such time as twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then resume bandaging if you see it needs doing, and hold it in place and leave it like that until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And she is restored within the most 28 days, and in some cases does not exceed even one month.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Sometimes it happens that the shoulder breaks or is wide at its end and not in the middle, and does not even extend as far as by touch;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you align it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the shoulder powder from the mill with plenty of eggs, and apply gentle bandages, and place two layers of cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and fine bandage, slightly larger than the shoulder, and where there is no movement on any part of the shoulder, use that hair from linen bandages so the bandage fits evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then it restrains everything tightly into one large bend, so that the limb does not move from its place, and he checks each link every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time when it dislocates, if it restrains, and puts the limb on equal footing if it is strong in its place, and lies the patient with their side on a table;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder has been healed after 20 days or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers have been completed, if it dislocates again and you are sure, because it is not an os that quickly takes hold lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone piece appears first and not below the knee, then proceed by removing it, along with the abscess beneath, and do as we have instructed for treating wounds of muscle dislocation.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The limb is broken only once in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the outer part.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it tilts downward and the patient feels intense pain throughout their body, along with loss of consciousness, immediately afterwards, and by chance vomits blood, and opens up the joints in the broken bones, and one can well perceive this.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And in restoration if the patient lies on his back and stomach, then put your hands under his shoulders, press down his shoulders, and join the ribs of the two ribs together, combine them at your hands, and with skill make it equal to all manners you can do this as long as the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place the plaster and cloths over the small salt pile, or another light stick, and wrap it in a cloth. Securely tie this around the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	Then round out the binding on the back, and strain it appropriately. Every hour check the tension of this bandage; if it relaxes, then tighten it again;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it seems necessary to loosen due to corrosion or itching that comes to the body, or pain or abscess, act quickly and loosen it. Remove the plaster, and treat with care whoever came into contact with it using appropriate remedies;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the plaster, and hold it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	The breaking of the ribs only comes about at their lower part near the back, and within them, and bend because they are spongy;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And one feels it very much during the examination in the way it should.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And for the healing process, you should make the break equal, just as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster and bind with a bandage if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of the ribs is occurring internally, one feels great pain and piercing in the body, akin to weeping, because the bone punctures the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And it causes pain in the kidneys, everywhere and vomiting of much blood, and this is serious illness, and they used to treat it with a large amount of food.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meats which swell the belly, in order to expel the wind from outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not follow this, for abscesses and pus do not come about unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And it is said that no one puts on the body suction cups for forming, as this appears reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt as to whether the suction cup attracts the excesses to the body due to its weakness in placement.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that when treating the wound of an animal, one should cover it with moist wool in a hot oil, and place the bandages between the ribs to make the healing consistent all around. Then follow the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels intense pain that cannot be borne by the bone piercing through the skin, there is doubt as to whether it's safe for the patient to cut through their broken rib area and then place an instrument to protect the lung.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone and gently drain it, and then stitch up the two edges of the wound if it's large, and treat with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if pus comes out from the abscesses, place oily bandages that have been moistened with rose oil on them, and place them on the wound;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the wound while applying what is suitable for pus, and place gentle supports on the rib area where it should be applied, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break at the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No breakage occurs at the bones of the neck, and it does not bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And similarly at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to any person, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, take care; if you see their hands softened, swollen, and dead, and unable to move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel.

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the breaking of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes the hip bone is broken, and if that happens, it might cause a small reduction in strength at the shoulder.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And they continue for quite some time, reducing it until the shoulder is eased, and there's a sharp pain at the broken spot, and it swells where the bone was broken.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	From the breaking of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulders are those that are between the collarbone and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you should restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The first one is to take a rod of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie with two shoulder straps, and lift them up, then position the patient on the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then put his broken arms on the rod until they reach the waist, and make a bend of the rod halfway, then lift him up or let the assistants extend him downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the brace so that it is evenly on both his hands until the splint returns as it should.

And the other method is that you place the patient on their back, and tie their hand to their neck, then instruct two assistants to have one cut off from where it's broken in his hands, and the other cuts off everything up to one finger length, stretching each one to its respective side.

And put the brace, and hold it to the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is straight up instead of hanging down, without anything preventing it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use these tools, and place one on the break larger and stronger than the others, and have two inches between each tool, and make sure every tool is large enough to pass through the fracture three inches from either side;

de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is made of two bones, which are called the "foscile" pair; one is small and it covers the pit.

par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance only the large foscile breaks, or only the small one, by chance they break together.

de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand

de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bones of the thigh are often broken; and well one sees this when they turn both forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And for the restoration, it is tying above the breakage, and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the muscles lie over this face, then stretch each minister's ligament to its equal part;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	This is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thumb, then one should apply the ligaments towards the knife, and the other ones over the breakage.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it's near the knee, then place its ligaments above the knee, and let its extension downwards;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then set the bones to their natural position with both hands, as long as it follows its natural shape, and then apply plaster, and the bandage, should there be any abscesses.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is pus at the wound, let it subside then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The labor is performed in an orderly manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the burn with a bandage folded two or three times, and keep the excess. Then turn the leg until the heels reach the base of the foot, and thread the first piece lengthwise between the cuff and the leg, under the knee and upwards; tie the end of the string above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then wrap the bandage around the leg and the calf, then place the stakes over the burn. Place a stake on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then use a loop of eight threads between the leg and calf of fabric to make an even pressure, then start to bind in turns of three or four around the burn;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And when you go further beyond the incision, and loosen less;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then open the two knots of the thread you have placed between the thigh and the calf, and tie three points that are above it. Then return under the body of the thread until you see beneath the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And hold it so that it doesn't move from its place, then leave it like this. Then until no further abscess appears or swelling or other sign occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, reset it and address what comes, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	And if there are pieces of bone that catch, then it is to your advantage to use force, as long as you can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if one cannot, then it is necessary to cut open the joint, and draw out force;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And treat as we have said, until it becomes clean.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And each time the heart is broken in such a way that one puts in the garlic, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Nevertheless, after this treatment made, there is no injury to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the flesh is restored within one day, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, depending on the variety of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee, there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it's usually just a crack, or it might be lost, causing pain in all injuries and being felt well by one.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration consists in making what is round at its ends equal until they move as can be done;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster, and if necessary, put a round garlic on it, and hold it in place as needed. Then reorder all the positions that we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses and similar conditions;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If faced with each accident, attend to what it requires of you, until your mind is clear.
de la brisure de la jambe	Regarding the breaking of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right "malleolus", and the other is called "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if any injury or break occurs like in the arm, treatment for it is similar to that of an arm, equally so; and the operations are all one. And if both bones of the leg are broken together, then the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then twist in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it clearly;
et torne desoz.	And it twists around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply extension, and set them equally, and fix the joints in place;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But still, it is necessary if the fracture is ugly, and there are many fragments, that the extension be smaller and more gentle;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and guide according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your task, take two wooden poles that harden and support the leg on both sides, and let them be as long as from the thigh down to the ankles;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap them both with cloths above and below, and tie in the middle as well, and at this binding, let neither leg droop to the right nor to the left, and thus it is well done.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And no one administers any bandage all the way down the leg, and it is made of wood, and you place the leg to guard against movement, and this is properly done in the fracture where there is injury;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move each leg every day to see if there's an abscess or any other incident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the treatment continues as long as it is effective.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones at the knee
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle it does not come from breaking, but when bones at the knee are broken, there is a break and in the legs, powerlessness occurs in multiple positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens with a bone in the foot fracture, and you see these bones mount one over the other, place the afflicted feet on the ground like they want to go, and then put your foot under his, where the bones are raised, press them so hard that their senses return in their legs;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and place it upwards, put a small table under the foot with two shoulders filled, then restrain at the foot on the opposite side, then when you have wrapped it in bandages around, and other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the bandage, for you will find that the bones are equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of his fingers are broken, if you restore them, just like we have said about the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place the broken finger at an angle corresponding to the length of the finger, and make it slightly wider; then set this over the board that I mentioned, and hold it firmly in place.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, broken, for each finger place an applicator according to its quantity, wrapped in a single layer of linen, and hold the board firmly in place.
